<userid>108177498255527674501< /userid>< name>
Casey J. Covenant</name>
<time>1482447424059< /time><rate>5</rate>< Review>
Truly Exceptional. I don't often write reviews as, to be honest, most places are between one and three stars with food so bad, uninspired or bland and I don't want to feel like I contributed to the demise of a small business, which leads me to normally remain silent. Delia's has possibly the best tacos Dorados  (fried hard shell) I have ever eaten and that salsa roja is almost unmatched with a perfect balance between spice, salt and lime. The refried beans are the perfect consistency and you can tell that they were homemade and finished off with a nice dusting of cotija cheese. I'll absolutely be back and can't wait to try the rest of the menu. Truly impressive!<//Review>

<Date>1566403428950<//Date><Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
Decided to give this place a try since I used to pass by it numerous times. Plus I was in a mood for Mexican food. It is conveniently located on York Blvd right next to the fire station. Not very hard to miss, especially if your driving. They do have parking an is super small, but street parking seems to not be an issue.  I love that they have a decorative outside seating area with plants and the shade from the trees nearby. So if you have a furry friend you're good to go. Decided to order sopes de carnitas, only order two since I thought they were going to be small. To my surprise they were not, not only that but also the meat was really tasty. I complimented the owner about the food and she was grateful and seem humble about it. I fell in love even more with the place. They stop service early so give them a call before you come so you get no surprises. I will continue to give this place my business since the service was great and food was up to part.< /Review>

Kelly Hirano<//user_name>
<time>1618202878326</time><Rating>5</Rating>< text>
Came here for shave ice with the family and it was awesome. From other pictures, it looks like they used to have the petal-plastic containers I remember from Hawaii, but they‚Äôve replaced them with more eco-friendly paper-based bowls. The ice shaving machine looks like the standard Hawaiian one and the ice itself comes out light and fluffy. About 16 flavors are available, limit 3 per serving. $4 for a small, $6 for a large and $3 for the unadvertised mini. Add $1 for a scoop of vanilla ice cream in the middle. Small is a generous size, pictured below.

Update (4/11/2021): Still delicious and the best shave ice I‚Äôve had outside of Hawaii. Mini is now advertised, small and large increased in price a little bit. Absolutely worth it. Inside dining is closed, so it‚Äôs either eat outside sitting on the brick walkway or take it somewhere else.<//text>

I moved in June of 2018 and had to down size from a 4200sq ft house to 1900sq ft house so I had to store half of my belongings. I looked around for the right storage facility a month before I moved and I chose South Bay Storage because of how secure the facility is and the cleanliness of the grounds. 102311347848274574247< /user_id>
< Text>
The food was excellent and our server (Jerome) was very attentive and helpful.  I had the duck breast with couscous and my girlfriend had the Black Cod.   The mushroom/manchego cheese appetizer was ok...seemed like the preparation was a little rushed.   They also have a great wine selection....but no bottles under $32.  The bottle we had Evodia (2009) was $38 but sells in the stores for $7.   I guess i just can't get over the high 500% mark up in restaurants.  It just seems a little a little extreme.

The ambiance was ok.  You can tell they're trying.   But the decor is a little conflicting.  It's a mix between modern and traditional.  The outdoor patio area is great....and they have heat lamps to keep it cozy and warm.  There's also a nice modern-style fire pit.     It's the inside that needs a little face lift to keep up with the modern/contemporary feel i believe they're trying to achieve.    Also, the television behind the bar is a bit distracting.  It's constantly on even when there is no game.

I gave it a 3 because the ambiance clash.   One of the main reasons I enjoy a restaurant is because of the ambiance.< /Text>

<Text>I came in on business with Musclepharm and I was greeted by friendly and attractive staff. I had never been to a golds gym before but had heard good things about them being the go to for heavier dumbells and a bodybuilding friendly environment.

There was a decent mix of ages but I would put the average age there to be late 30's. From my conversations there I would say the crowd was rather well informed about nutrition and supplements.

The gym is definitely older, but I found the equipmemt to be in working order with great mix of classic and newer equipment. There was more equipment in then gym than expected. Floor space there is utilized very efficiently.

Highlights would include:
1. 150lb+ dumbells
2. Adjustable Deadlifting platform
3. Bumper plates and a rubber platform for Olympic lifts
4. Outdoor patio with weights and furniture.
5. Separate room for cardio equipment and a dance studio.
6. Its one of the three corporate Gold's gyms in Cali. So an "All club" membership from them($50ish/month) would also give u access to the Venice and Long Beach gyms. All other Golds gyms in Cali are franchises and cant offer access to the Venice club(the mecca of bb'ing).</Text>< Pics>

< Review>
I've been here multiple times for birthdays, girl night outs and going away parties. There are two areas in this club. The bar area where people can dance usually has hip hop and r&b music. This area also has booths for bottle service. And the actual dancefloor is usually top 40 or EDM music with all of the lights. My friends and I always have a good time here and there is something for everyone! The women's bathroom is cramped and small with two stalls but that's always the case in clubs.< /Review>

< Text>
Came here Friday night with my girlfriend. It was already midnight when we got there so it was just at that cusp between boring empty and uncomfortably full which was great. Seemed like there was no dress code even though it's advertised and a 5 dollar cover. It's not big inside but there's plenty of space to dance. In the middle is like a table that runs the length of the bar to put drinks on. The drinks where decently cheap and very strong which I loved. Whom ever they had DJing last night was killing it though , the crowd was going crazy with every song he mixed it , it was great. At some point in the night we left and I left my card and Id. When I went back to get it the doors where closed but I knocked and got the owner who was super nice , asked me to come in , got my name and returned my ID and credit card. Would come back!<//Text>

<Rate>3<//Rate><review>The average steak dinner is $50 and that's a 9oz filet & a slice of garlic bread.

Sides are not part of your meal.  Those are priced individually, which adds considerably to the cost.  One of our dinner guests actually said, after looking the menu over, "Oh.  Salad, beans and potatoes are $12 more, which should have been included anyway."  We laughed about it - but he was right.

Onion rings are provided for the table while you wait for your food and choice of ice cream or liqueur after dinner.  (If asked, we still would have preferred the sides to be included with the meal instead of these offerings).

There was a musician playing in the bar.  The music was audible to those of us in the dining room.  He was exceptionally good and we enjoyed it.  The atmosphere was casual and relaxed.

There is a view of the ocean but their windows were noticeably dirty and in need of a good cleaning.  Overall, everyone had a good time.< /review>< Pictures>

< Review>
This is a heartbreaker to write, because if I was doing this review 2 years ago, I'd be at 5 stars.

My wife and I were at F. McLintock's in early April and we definitely noticed the downhill slide that has taken place since the pandemic.  Everything seems to have been monetized here in the same way that steakhouses in SF and LA nickel-dime you for everything- it's all a-la-carte now.

Also, gone are the baked potatoes.  Seriously, how do you have a steakhouse and not have baked potatoes?  What's with that?

It breaks my heart to write this, but bang for the buck? You're better off going somewhere else.< /Review>

< Text>
I've been going here for years, but when I went yesterday, it just wasn't right.

The biggest problem was the water. It tasted like mildew or mold. I thought it just might be the glass, but my wife's water tasted the same. This is a place where you want to drink the water because the waiters do pouring tricks (pour blindfolded so the the glass on your head, or just pour really high). My steak sauce also had a hint of this flavor (so I assume they used water in making it).

My steak was good, but it was overcooked. I ordered medium-rare but it was more in the medium to medium-well category.

The service here was first rate as always, but the water killed it. I'm surprised I don't see any other reviews talking about this.</Text>

< Review>
Had been here 12 yrs ago and everything was great. This time, not so much. It wss a Tuesday evening, mid-August

Food -
The steak was excellent. The potatoes and onion rings were just right. But the bread and vegetables were poorly prepared. The beans should have been described better (spicy and dry vs sweet and tender) - i liked them, but my bf would have substituted them for a salad IF salad was an option. (And why isnt it?)

Environment:
Every few minutes a waitress would walk by hollering numbers, and the other staff would holler back. I guess it's "cute", but right in my ear was unnerving. Can't blame them for the screaming (literally) toddlers, but it made the visit a very unpleasant for the price, especially with the bussing station being centrally located - dishes being slammed around loudly...Wait staff was very kind.
The steak was not enough to make up for the rest, but maybe we hit them on an off day.<//Review>

< Time>
1478717409917</Time>
<review>This place was probably good twenty years ago, and I have no idea how they have so many good reviews now.

The decor is decrepit. The interior is dark and smells. The taxidermied animals are dirty and have obviously seen much better days. The tables and chairs are worn, and the carpeting is badly stained and in need of replacing.

The restaurant is understaffed, and the workers clearly do not put much effort into their jobs. The "hostess" said that it would be a few minutes and disappeared for about ten. She came back to greet a couple who had been waiting for several minutes and had a reservation. She disappeared with them and came back from the restaurant to grab menus and said, "I can take you now," as if it were an inconvenience.

There were several large parties, and the servers were clearly more interested in working those tables. A group with four children was sat with the kids across from us, instead of with them at the opposite end, bothering nobody. This removed any remaining appeal to the ambience.

The food is below average and very over-priced. My partner got the top sirloin. Even though it was cooked as directed, it was very tough. Although she was craving the meat, she simply couldn't force herself to eat all of it. She did enjoy the beans, which were spicy to her liking.

I ordered the pork chop. It was was also very tough and slightly dry. It lacked the strap of fat that should have made it moist and tasty. It came with a small bowl of cold applesauce, served as if just spooned out of the can in the fridge. Caramelize apples would have been a better match, fresh, and served warm. The rice pilaf was not nearly as good as stuff that you can get from a box.

The potatoes served with the meal were amazingly bland. I am one who generally prefers quite bland food, but had to make two rounds with the salt and pepper. The smattering of onions at the bottom were really the tastiest part of the potatoes.

The bread service was underwhelming. The basket only had two pieces of bread for two people. How long was that supposed to last? The bread itself was greasy and flat.

The sherbet was ridiculous. First, the word has only one "R" in it. The servers should know. Second, rainbow sherbet has more than just lime and a smattering of raspberry. The sherbet came in difficult to handle metal cups and clearly had been scooped earlier and then put back in the freezer. There were ice crystals in the bottom.

Finally, we had to wait a considerable amount of time for the bill. The credit card receipt came back with a felt tip pen to sign.

If the prices had been much lower, this might have slid by as acceptable tourist fare. However, for what they are charging, the food should be spot on and the service good.

I strongly suggest avoiding McClintock's. I don't think that it even qualifies as a bar pretending to be a restaurant. There are many better options nearby.<//review>< pictures>
None< /pictures>
< Name>
Jamie C<//Name>

Pretty bummed out so we decided to get the nachos but then soon to find out that they were out of nachos for the evening. Pretty bummed out about our second choice . Looking at the menu and nothing else really looked good for my appetite.
